Utah Code Annotated - Title 53F - Public Education System -- Funding
====================================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 53F - Chapter 1 - Title Provisions
**************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-101(1): This title is known as "Public Education System -- Funding."
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-101(2): This chapter is known as "Title Provisions."


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-102 Public education code definitions.
------------------------------------------------------------------
The terms defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-103 Title 53F definitions.
------------------------------------------------------


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104 Education monitoring and funds management.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(1)(a): "Allocable cost" means a cost for goods or services that are chargeable or assignable to a state award or cost objective in accordance with relative benefits an LEA receives.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(1)(b): "Reasonable cost" means a cost that, in nature and amount, does not exceed an amount that a prudent person would incur under the circumstances prevailing at the time the decision was made to incur the cost.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(1)(c): "State award" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(1)(c)(i): money that the Legislature appropriates to state education programs for an LEA's use; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(1)(c)(ii): a grant that the state board awards to an LEA as part of a state education program.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(2): Except as otherwise provided in this public education code, the state board shall monitor state-funded education programs and the expenditure of state funds in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(3): Except as otherwise authorized by statute, the state board shall not allow a cost under state awards, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(3)(a): the cost is necessary and reasonable for, and allocable to, the performance of the state award;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(3)(b): the cost conforms to any limitations or exclusions that apply uniformly to the LEA's other activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(3)(c): the LEA accorded the cost consistent treatment among programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(3)(d): the LEA determined the cost in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(3)(e): the LEA adequately documented the cost; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(3)(f): the LEA incurred the cost during the approved budget period.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4): In determining whether a cost is a reasonable cost, the state board shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(a): whether the cost is of a type generally recognized as ordinary for:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(a)(i): the operation of the LEA; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(a)(ii): the proper and efficient performance of the state award;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(b): the restraints or requirements imposed by:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(b)(i): sound business practices;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(b)(ii): arm's length bargaining;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(b)(iii): federal, state, local, tribal, or other laws and regulations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(b)(iv): the state award's restrictions and conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(c): market prices for comparable goods or services in the geographic area;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(d): whether an individual involved in a decision to incur the cost acted with prudence in the circumstances considering the individual's responsibilities to:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(d)(i): the LEA;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(d)(ii): the LEA's employees;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(d)(iii): the LEA's students;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(d)(iv): the public; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(d)(v): the state government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(4)(e): whether the LEA significantly deviated from the LEA's established practices and policies concerning incurring costs so that the costs the LEA incurs for the performance of the state award are unjustifiably increased.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(5): The state board shall determine that a cost is an allocable cost if:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(5)(a): the LEA incurred the cost specifically for the state award;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(5)(b): the cost:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(5)(b)(i): benefits both the state award and the LEA's other work; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(5)(b)(ii): can be distributed in proportions that may be approximated using reasonable methods; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-1-104(5)(c): the cost is necessary to the overall operation of the LEA and is assignable in part to the state award.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 53F - Chapter 2 - State Funding -- Minimum School Program
*************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "State Funding -- Minimum School Program."

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(1): "Basic state-supported school program," "basic program," or "basic school program" means public education programs for kindergarten, elementary, and secondary school students that are operated and maintained for the amount derived by multiplying the number of weighted pupil units for each school district or charter school by the value established each year in the enacted public education budget, except as otherwise provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(2): "LEA governing board" means a local school board or charter school governing board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(3): "Pupil in average daily membership" or "ADM" means a full-day equivalent pupil.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4): (4); (4)(c); (4)(d)(i); Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act; (4)(d); (4)(d); (4)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(a): (4) "Minimum School Program" means the state-supported public school programs for kindergarten, elementary, and secondary schools as described in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(b): The Minimum School Program established in school districts and charter schools shall include the equivalent of a school term of nine months as determined by the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(c)(i): The state board shall establish the number of days or equivalent instructional hours that school is held for an academic school year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(c)(ii): Education, enhanced by utilization of technologically enriched delivery systems, when approved by an LEA governing board, shall receive full support by the state board as it pertains to fulfilling the attendance requirements, excluding time spent viewing commercial advertising.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d): (4)(c); (4)(d)(i); Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act; (4)(d); (4)(d); (4)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d)(i): (4)(c) An LEA governing board may reallocate up to 32 instructional hours or four school days established under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d)(ii)(A): at which a quorum of the LEA governing board is present; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d)(ii)(B): Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act held in compliance with
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d)(iii): (4)(d) If an LEA governing board reallocates instructional hours or school days as provided by this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d)(iii)(A): 90 days before the beginning of the school year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d)(iii)(B): for the 2021-2022 and 2022-2023 school years, due to circumstances within the LEA or a given school due to the COVID-19 pandemic, at least 14 calendar days before the reallocated instructional hours or school days.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(d)(iv): (4)(d); (4)(b) Instructional hours or school days reallocated for teacher preparation time or teacher professional development pursuant to this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(e): The Minimum School Program includes a program or allocation funded by a line item appropriation or other appropriation designated as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(e)(i): Basic School Program;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(e)(ii): Related to Basic Programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(e)(iii): Voted and Board Levy Programs; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(4)(e)(iv): Minimum School Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-102(5): "Weighted pupil unit or units or WPU or WPUs" means the unit of measure of factors that is computed in accordance with this chapter for the purpose of determining the costs of a program on a uniform basis for each school district or charter school.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-103 Purpose of chapter.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-103(1): The purpose of this chapter is to provide a minimum school program for the state in accordance with the constitutional mandate.  It recognizes that all children of the state are entitled to reasonably equal educational opportunities regardless of their place of residence in the state and of the economic situation of their respective school districts or other agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-103(2): It further recognizes that although the establishment of an educational system is primarily a state function, school districts should be required to participate on a partnership basis in the payment of a reasonable portion of the cost of a minimum program.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-103(3): It is also the purpose of this chapter to describe the manner in which the state and the school districts shall pay their respective share of the costs of a minimum program.  This chapter also recognizes that each locality should be empowered to provide educational facilities and opportunities beyond the minimum program and accordingly provide a method whereby that latitude of action is permitted and encouraged.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-204 Use of funds for approved programs -- Assessment of funded programs.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-204(1): Funds appropriated under this chapter shall only be used for programs approved by the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-204(2): The state board shall assess the progress and degree of effectiveness of all programs funded under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-207 Loss in student enrollment -- Board action.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
To avoid penalizing a school district financially for an excessive loss in student enrollment due to factors beyond its control, the state board may allow a percentage increase in units otherwise allowable during any year when a school district's average daily membership drops more than 4% below the average for the highest two of the preceding three years in the school district.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-209 Limited LEA budgetary flexibility.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302 Determination of weighted pupil units.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(1): (5) The number of weighted pupil units in the Minimum School Program for each year is the total of the units for each school district and, subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(2): The number of weighted pupil units is computed by adding the average daily membership of all pupils of the school district or charter school attending schools, other than self-contained classes for children with a disability.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(3): (3)(b); 53F-2-302
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(3)(a): (3)(b) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(3)(b): 53F-2-302 The number of weighted pupil units is computed by multiplying the average daily membership for the number of students who are enrolled in kindergarten for less than the equivalent length of the schedule for grades 1 through 3, based on the October 1 data described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(4)(a): The state board shall use prior year plus growth to determine average daily membership in distributing money under the Minimum School Program where the distribution is based on kindergarten through grade 12 ADMs or weighted pupil units.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(4)(b): Under prior year plus growth, kindergarten through grade 12 average daily membership for the current year is based on the actual kindergarten through grade 12 average daily membership for the previous year plus an estimated percentage growth factor.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(4)(c): The growth factor is the percentage increase in total average daily membership on the first school day of October in the current year as compared to the total average daily membership on the first school day of October of the previous year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(5): (3)(b) In distributing funds to charter schools under this section, charter school pupils shall be weighted, where applicable, as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(5)(a): (3)(b) except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(5)(b): .99 for pupils in grades 7 through 8; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-302(5)(c): 1.2 for pupils in grades 9 through 12.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304 Necessarily existent small schools -- Computing additional weighted pupil units -- Consolidation of small schools.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(1): As used in this section, "necessarily existent small schools funding balance" means the difference between:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(1)(a): the amount appropriated for the necessarily existent small schools program in a fiscal year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(1)(b): the amount distributed to school districts for the necessarily existent small schools program in the same fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(2): (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(2)(a): (3) Upon application by a local school board, the state board shall, in consultation with the local school board, classify schools in the school district as necessarily existent small schools, in accordance with this section and state board rules adopted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(2)(b): An application must be submitted to the state board before April 2, and the state board must report a decision to a local school board before June 2.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The state board shall adopt standards and make rules, in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(3)(a): govern the approval of necessarily existent small schools consistent with principles of efficiency and economy that serve the purpose of eliminating schools where consolidation is feasible by participation in special school units; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(3)(b): ensure that school districts are not building secondary schools in close proximity to one another where economy and efficiency would be better served by one school meeting the needs of secondary students in a designated geographical area.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(4): The state board shall prepare and publish objective standards and guidelines for determining which small schools are necessarily existent after consultation with local school boards.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(a): Additional weighted pupil units for schools classified as necessarily existent small schools shall be computed using distribution formulas adopted by the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(b): The distribution formulas establish the following maximum sizes for funding under the necessarily existent small school program:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(b)(i): an elementary school
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(b)(ii): a one or two-year secondary school
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(b)(iii): a three-year secondary school
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(b)(iv): a four-year secondary school
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(b)(v): a six-year secondary school
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(c): An elementary school with fewer than 10 students shall receive the same add-on weighted pupil units as an elementary school with 10 students.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(d): A secondary school with fewer than 15 students shall receive the same add-on weighted pupil units as a secondary school with 15 students.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(e): If a necessarily existent small school generates ADM in both elementary and secondary grades, the state board may divide the school's ADM between an elementary and secondary distribution formula.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(5)(f): The state board shall prepare and distribute an allocation table based on the distribution formula to each school district.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(6)(a): To avoid penalizing a school district financially for consolidating the school district's small schools, additional weighted pupil units may be allowed a school district each year, not to exceed two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(6)(b): The additional weighted pupil units may not exceed the difference between what the school district receives for a consolidated school and what the school district would have received for the small schools had the small schools not been consolidated.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(7): (7)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(7)(a): The state board may allocate up to 208 weighted pupil units to support schools that:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(7)(a)(i): have isolating conditions, as defined by the state board, including geographic isolation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(7)(a)(ii): do not qualify for necessarily existent small schools funding due to formula limitations.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(7)(b): (7) The state board shall review funding allocations under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(8): If the state board classifies a school as a necessarily existent small school in accordance with this section, the state board shall, subject to legislative appropriation, distribute small district base funding to the relevant school district in the following amounts:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(8)(a): for a district with 500 students or less, 83 additional weighted pupil units;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(8)(b): for a district with 501 to 1,000 students, 28 additional weighted pupil units; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(8)(c): for a district with 1,001 to 2,000 students, 14 additional weighted pupil units.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-304(9): 53G-6-305(3)(a) Subject to legislative appropriation, the state board shall give first priority from an appropriation made under this section to funding an expense approved by the state board as described in Subsection

Sec. 300.208.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(3)(d)(ii): An LEA may not use state special education program money to supplant other state funds, local funds, or federal funds.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(ii): The special education student growth factor is calculated by comparing total special education average daily membership of one year previous to the current year to the total special education average daily membership two years previous to the current year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(iii): When calculating and applying the growth factor, a school district's total special education ADM for a given year is limited to the following percentage of the school district's total student ADM for the same year:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(iii)(A): for a school district in a county of the first, second, or third class, 14%; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(iii)(B): for a school district in a county of the fourth, fifth, or sixth class, 20%.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(iv): Growth ADMs are calculated by applying the growth factor to the total special education average daily membership of one year previous to the current year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(v): Growth ADMs for each school district or each charter school are multiplied by the following weighted pupil units and added to the prior year special education add-on WPU to determine each school district's or each charter school's total allocation:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(v)(A): for fiscal year 2023, 1.35 weighted pupil units;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(v)(B): for fiscal year 2024, 1.15 weighted pupil units; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(7)(e)(v)(C): beginning in fiscal year 2025, and every fiscal year thereafter, 1.00 weighted pupil units.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-307(8): If money appropriated under this chapter for programs for students with disabilities does not meet the costs of LEAs for those programs, each LEA shall first receive the amount generated for each student with a disability under the basic program.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308 Preschool special education appropriation -- Extended year program appropriation -- Appropriation for special education programs in state institutions -- Appropriations for stipends for special educators.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(1)(a): Money appropriated to the state board for the preschool special education program shall be allocated to school districts to provide a free, appropriate public education to preschool students with a disability, ages three through five.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(1)(b): The money shall be distributed on the basis of the school district's count of preschool children with a disability for December 1 of the previous year, as mandated by federal law.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(2): Money appropriated for the extended school year program for children with a severe disability shall be limited to students with severe disabilities with education program goals identifying significant regression and recoupment disability as approved by the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(3)(a): Money appropriated for self-contained regular special education programs may not be used to supplement other school programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(3)(b): Money in any of the other restricted line item appropriations may not be reduced more than 2% to be used for purposes other than those specified by the appropriation, unless otherwise provided by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(4)(a): The state board shall compute preschool funding by a factor of 1.47 times the current December 1 child count of eligible preschool aged three, four, and five-year-olds times the WPU value, limited to 8% growth over the prior year December 1 count.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(4)(b): The state board shall develop guidelines to implement the funding formula for preschool special education, and establish prevalence limits for distribution of the money.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-308(5): 53F-2-310 Of the money appropriated for Special Education - State Programming, the state board shall distribute the revenue generated from 909 WPUs to school districts, charter schools, and the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind for stipends to special educators for additional days of work pursuant to the requirements of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310 Stipends for special educators for additional days of work.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1)(a): "Special education teacher" means a teacher whose primary assignment is the instruction of students with disabilities who are eligible for special education services.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1)(b): "Special educator" means a person employed by a school district, charter school, or the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind who holds:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1)(b)(i): a license issued by the state board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1)(b)(ii): a position as a:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1)(b)(ii)(A): special education teacher;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1)(b)(ii)(B): speech-language pathologist; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(1)(b)(ii)(C): teacher of the deaf or hard of hearing;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(2): The Legislature shall annually appropriate money for stipends to special educators for additional days of work:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(2)(a): in recognition of the added duties and responsibilities assumed by special educators to comply with federal law regulating the education of students with disabilities and the need to attract and retain qualified special educators; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(2)(b): subject to future budget constraints.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(3)(a): The state board shall distribute money appropriated under this section to school districts, charter schools, and the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind for stipends for special educators in the amount of $200 per day for up to 10 additional working days.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(3)(b): Money distributed under this section shall include, in addition to the $200 per day stipend, money for the following employer-paid benefits:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(3)(b)(i): retirement;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(3)(b)(ii): workers' compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(3)(b)(iii): Social Security; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(3)(b)(iv): Medicare.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4): A special educator receiving a stipend shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(a): work an additional day beyond the number of days contracted with the special educator's school district or school for each daily stipend;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(b): schedule the additional days of work before or after the school year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(c): use the additional days of work to perform duties related to the IEP process, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(c)(i): administering student assessments;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(c)(ii): conducting IEP meetings;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(c)(iii): writing IEPs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(c)(iv): conferring with parents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(4)(c)(v): maintaining records and preparing reports.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(5): A special educator may:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(5)(a): elect to receive a stipend for one to 10 days of additional work; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(5)(b): elect to not receive a stipend.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-310(6): A person who does not hold a full-time position as a special educator is eligible for a partial stipend equal to the percentage of a full-time special educator position the person assumes.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312 Appropriation for class size reduction.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(1): Money appropriated to the state board for class size reduction shall be used to reduce the average class size in kindergarten through grade 8 in the state's public schools.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(2): 53F-2-302 A school district or charter school shall receive an allocation for class size reduction based on the school district or charter school's prior year average daily membership plus growth in kindergarten through grade 8 as determined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(3): (3)(b); (3)(b)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(3)(a): (3)(b) An LEA governing board may use an allocation to reduce class size in any one or all of the grades referred to under this section, except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(3)(b): (3)(b)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(3)(b)(i): An LEA governing board shall use 50% of an allocation to reduce class size in any one or all of grades kindergarten through grade 2, with an emphasis on improving student reading skills.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(3)(b)(ii): (3)(b)(i) If a school district's or charter school's average class size is below 18 students in kindergarten through grade 2, an LEA governing board may petition the state board for, and the state board may grant, a waiver of the requirement described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(4): A school may use nontraditional innovative and creative methods to reduce class sizes with this appropriation and may use part of an allocation to focus on class size reduction for specific groups, such as at risk students, or for specific blocks of time during the school day.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(5)(a): An LEA governing board may use up to 20% of an allocation under this section for capital facilities projects if such projects would help to reduce class size.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(5)(b): If a school district's or charter school's student population increases by at least 5% or at least 700 students from the previous school year, the LEA governing board may use up to 50% of an allocation received by the school district or charter school under this section for classroom construction.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(6): This appropriation is to supplement any other appropriation made for class size reduction.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-312(7): The Legislature shall provide for an annual adjustment in the appropriation authorized under this section in proportion to the increase in the number of students in the state in kindergarten through grade 8.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-314(2)(a)(ii)(B): for each student with limited English proficiency, up to .1 total weighted pupil units.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403 Eligibility for state-supported transportation -- Approved bus routes.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(1): A student eligible for state-supported transportation means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(1)(a): a student enrolled in kindergarten through grade 6 who lives at least 1-1/2 miles from school;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(1)(b): a student enrolled in grades 7 through 12 who lives at least two miles from school; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(1)(c): a student enrolled in a special program offered by a school district and approved by the state board for trainable, motor, multiple-disability, or other students with severe disabilities who are incapable of walking to school or where it is unsafe for students to walk because of their disabling condition, without reference to distance from school.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(2): If a school district implements double sessions as an alternative to new building construction, with the approval of the state board, those affected elementary school students residing less than 1-1/2 miles from school may be transported one way to or from school because of safety factors relating to darkness or other hazardous conditions as determined by the local school board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3): (3)(b)(ii); 53F-2-402(3); 53F-2-402(3)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(a): The state board shall distribute transportation money to school districts based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(a)(i): an allowance per mile for approved bus routes;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(a)(ii): an allowance per hour for approved bus routes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(a)(iii): a minimum allocation for each school district eligible for transportation funding.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(b): (3)(b)(ii); 53F-2-402(3); 53F-2-402(3)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(b)(i): (3)(b)(ii); 53F-2-402(3) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(b)(ii): 53F-2-402(3) The state board shall distribute state appropriations for transportation for fiscal years 2021 and 2022 using fiscal year 2019 eligible transportation costs described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(3)(c): The state board shall annually review the allowance per mile and the allowance per hour and adjust the allowances to reflect current economic conditions.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(4)(a): Approved bus routes for funding purposes shall be determined on fall data collected by October 1.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(4)(b): Approved route funding shall be determined on the basis of the most efficient and economic routes.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(5): A Transportation Advisory Committee with representation from school district superintendents, business officials, school district transportation supervisors, and state board employees shall serve as a review committee for addressing school transportation needs, including recommended approved bus routes.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-403(6): A local school board may provide for the transportation of students regardless of the distance from school, from general funds of the school district.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411 Appropriation for Title I Schools in Improvement Paraeducators Program.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(1): (3) As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(1)(a): "Eligible school" means a Title I school that has not achieved adequate yearly progress, as defined in the No Child Left Behind Act of 2001, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 6301 et seq. in the same subject area for two consecutive years.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(1)(b): (3) "Paraeducator" means a school employee who:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(1)(b)(i): delivers instruction under the direct supervision of a teacher; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(1)(b)(ii): (3) meets the requirements under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(1)(c): "Program" means the Title I Schools in Improvement Paraeducators Program created in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(2): The program is created to provide funding for eligible schools to hire paraeducators to provide additional instructional aid in the classroom to assist students in achieving academic success and assist the school in exiting Title I school improvement status.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(3): A paraeducator who is funded under this section shall have:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(3)(a): earned a secondary school diploma or a recognized equivalent;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(3)(b)(i): completed at least two years with a minimum of 48 semester hours at an accredited higher education institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(3)(b)(ii): obtained an associates or higher degree from an accredited higher education institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(3)(b)(iii): satisfied a rigorous state or local assessment about the individual's knowledge of, and ability to assist in instructing students in, reading, writing, and mathematics; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(3)(c): received large group-, small group-, and individual-level professional development that is intensive and focused and covers curriculum, instruction, assessment, classroom and behavior management, and teaming.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(4): The state board shall distribute money appropriated for the program to eligible schools, in accordance with rules adopted by the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-411(5): Funds appropriated under the program may not be used to supplant other money used for paraeducators at eligible schools.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-421 Flexible allocation.
----------------------------------------------------
Subject to appropriations, the state board shall distribute funds in the MSP flexible allocation on a WPU basis resulting in LEAs receiving funding proportional to the number of WPUs the LEA generates under the Basic School Program.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502 Dual language immersion.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(1): 53B-1-201 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(1)(a): "Dual language immersion" means an instructional setting in which a student receives a portion of instruction in English and a portion of instruction exclusively in a partner language.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(1)(b): "Local education agency" or "LEA" means a school district or a charter school.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(1)(c): "Participating LEA" means an LEA selected by the state board to receive a grant described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(1)(d): "Partner language" means a language other than English in which instruction is provided in dual language immersion.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(1)(e): 53B-1-201 "Restricted foreign entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The state board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(a): establish a dual language immersion program;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(b)(i): a grant program for an LEA to receive funding for dual language immersion;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(b)(ii): the required qualifications for an LEA to be a participating LEA;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(b)(iii): subject to this section, requirements of a participating LEA;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(b)(iv): a proficiency assessment for each partner language; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(b)(v): a progression of how a school in a participating LEA adds grade levels in which the school offers dual language immersion; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(c): subject to legislative appropriations:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(c)(i): select participating LEAs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(2)(c)(ii): award to a participating LEA a grant to support dual language immersion in the LEA.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(3): (2)(b); (2)(b)(iv) A participating LEA shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(3)(a): establish in a school a full-day dual language immersion instructional model that provides at least 50% of instruction exclusively in a partner language;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(3)(b): (2)(b) in accordance with the state board rules described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(3)(c): (2)(b)(iv) annually administer to each student in grades 3 through 8 who participates in dual language immersion an assessment described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(4): (2)(a); (4)(b) The state board shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(4)(a)(i): offering professional learning for dual language immersion educators;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(4)(a)(ii): developing curriculum related to dual language immersion; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-502(4)(a)(iii): providing instructional support for a partner language;

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504 Teacher Salary Supplement Program.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(a): "Eligible teacher" means a teacher who:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(a)(i): has a qualifying educational background or qualifying teaching background;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(a)(ii): has a supplement-approved assignment that corresponds to the teacher's qualifying educational background or qualifying teaching background;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(a)(iii): qualifies for the teacher's supplement-approved assignment in accordance with state board rule; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(a)(iv): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(a)(iv)(A): is a new employee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(a)(iv)(B): has not received an unsatisfactory rating on the teacher's three most recent evaluations.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(b): "Field of computer science" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(b)(i): computer science; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(b)(ii): computer information technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(c): "Field of science" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(c)(i): integrated science;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(c)(ii): chemistry;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(c)(iii): physics;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(c)(iv): physical science; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(c)(v): general science.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d): "Qualifying educational background" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(i): for a teacher who is assigned a secondary school level mathematics course:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(i)(A): a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree in mathematics; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(i)(B): a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree that has course requirements that are substantially equivalent to the course requirements for a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree in mathematics;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(ii): for a teacher who is assigned a grade 7 or 8 integrated science course, chemistry course, or physics course:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(ii)(A): a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree in a field of science; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(ii)(B): a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree that has course requirements that are substantially equivalent to the course requirements of those required for a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree in a field of science;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(iii): for a teacher who is assigned a computer science course:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(iii)(A): a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree in a field of computer science; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(iii)(B): a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree that has course requirements that are substantially equivalent to the course requirements of those required for a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree in a field of computer science; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(d)(iv): for a teacher who is assigned to teach special education, a bachelor's degree major, master's degree, or doctoral degree in special education.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(e): "Qualifying teaching background" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(e)(i): the teacher has been teaching the same supplement-approved assignment in Utah public schools for at least 10 years; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(e)(ii): the teacher has a professional deaf education license issued by the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(f): "Supplement-approved assignment" means an assignment to teach:

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(f)(ii): integrated science in grade 7 or 8;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(f)(iii): chemistry;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(f)(iv): physics;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(f)(v): computer science;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(f)(vi): special education; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-504(1)(f)(vii): deaf education.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-506(1): (1)(b)(ii) As used in this section:

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705 Grants for charter school start-up costs.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(1)(a): The State Charter School Board shall use money appropriated for charter school start-up costs to provide grants to charter schools to pay for expenses for the planning and implementation of a charter school.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(1)(b): The State Charter School Board:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(1)(b)(i): may use up to 8% of the money appropriated for charter school start-up costs for financial monitoring of new charter schools and to provide professional development or technical assistance for charter school governing board members and staff of new charter schools; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(1)(b)(ii): in accordance with rules adopted by the state board, may use up to $200,000 of the money appropriated for charter school start-up costs for a mentoring program for new and existing charter schools.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(2): The amount of a grant for charter school start-up costs shall be based on the authorized enrollment of the charter school.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(3): The state board shall make rules consistent with this section specifying:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(3)(a): procedures for applying for and awarding grants for charter school start-up costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(3)(b): permitted uses of grant money; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(3)(c): requirements for a charter school to submit the following to the State Charter School Board:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(3)(c)(i): a budget for the grant money; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(3)(c)(ii): a final report on the expenditure of the grant money.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-705(4): The state board shall make rules establishing a mentoring program for new and existing charter schools.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-706 Small charter school base funding.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-706(1): Subject to legislative appropriation, the state board shall distribute small charter school base funding to charter schools with 2,000 or fewer students in the amount of the greater of $40,000 or $115 per student.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-706(2): A charter school's eligibility for small charter school base funding is determined by the charter school's student enrollment on October 1 of a given year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-2-706(3): Notwithstanding this section and subject to legislative appropriations, the state board may distribute to charter schools, regardless of size, one-time funding that the Legislature appropriates to mitigate funding losses as described in legislative appropriations.

--------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(1): 53F-2-102 "ADM" or "pupil in average daily membership" is as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(2): "Base tax effort rate" means the average of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(2)(a): the highest combined capital levy rate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(2)(b): the average combined capital levy rate for the school districts statewide.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(3): 11-14-310; 53F-8-402; 53F-8-303; 11-14-310 "Combined capital levy rate" means a rate that includes the sum of the following property tax levies:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(3)(a): 11-14-310; 53F-8-402
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(3)(a)(i): 11-14-310 the debt service levy authorized in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(3)(a)(ii): 53F-8-402 the voted capital outlay leeway authorized in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(3)(b): 53F-8-303; 11-14-310
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(3)(b)(i): 53F-8-303 the capital local levy authorized in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(3)(b)(ii): 11-14-310 the debt service levy authorized in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(4): (4)(a) "Derived net taxable value" means the quotient of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(4)(a): the total property tax collections from April 1 through the following March 31 for a school district for the calendar year preceding the March 31 date; divided by
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(4)(b): (4)(a) the school district's total tax rate for the calendar year preceding the March 31 referenced in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(5): "Highest combined capital levy rate" means the highest combined capital levy rate imposed by a school district within the state for a fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(6): "Property tax base per ADM" means the quotient of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(6)(a): a school district's derived net taxable value; divided by
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(6)(b): the school district's ADM.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(7): "Property tax yield per ADM" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(7)(a): the product of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(7)(a)(i): a school district's derived net taxable value; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(7)(a)(ii): the base tax effort rate; divided by
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(7)(b): the school district's ADM.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(8): "Statewide average property tax base per ADM" means the quotient of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(8)(a): the sum of all school districts' derived net taxable value; divided by
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-102(8)(b): the sum of all school districts' ADM.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-201 Capital outlay programs -- Use of funds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
A school district may only use the money provided under this chapter for school district capital outlay and debt service purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202 Capital Outlay Foundation Program created -- Distribution formulas -- Allocations.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202(1): 53F-3-202 As used in this section:

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202(1)(c): "Small school district" means a school district that has fewer than 1,000 pupils in average daily membership.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202(2): There is created the Capital Outlay Foundation Program to provide capital outlay funding to a school district based on a district's local property tax effort and property tax yield per student compared to a foundation guarantee funding level.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202(3):

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202(3)(b)(iii): derived net taxable value.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202(5): (3) If a qualifying school district imposes a combined capital levy rate that is greater than or equal to the base tax effort rate, the state board shall allocate to the qualifying school district an amount equal to the product of the following:

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-202(6)(c)(ii): the base tax effort rate.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-3-203(1)(b)(ii): has a property tax base per ADM in the year two years prior that is less than two times the statewide average property tax base per ADM in the year two years prior.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(1): "Assessment team" means a team consisting of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(1)(a): the student's parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(1)(b): the student's private school classroom teacher;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(1)(c): special education personnel from the student's school district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(1)(d): if available, special education personnel from the private school at which the student is enrolled.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(2): 53F-4-303 "Eligible private school" means a private school that meets the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(3): "Local Education Agency" or "LEA" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(3)(a): a school district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(3)(b): a charter school.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(4): "Preschool" means an education program for a student who:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(4)(a): is age three, four, or five; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(4)(b): has not entered kindergarten.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(5): "Scholarship student" means a student who receives a scholarship under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301(6): "Value of the weighted pupil unit" means the amount established each year in statute that is multiplied by the number of weighted pupil units to yield the funding level for the basic state-supported school program.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5 Findings and purpose.
-------------------------------------------------------
The Legislature finds that:Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(1): the state system of public education as established and maintained under the state constitution shall be open to all children of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(2): students with disabilities have special needs that merit educational alternatives which will allow students to learn in an appropriate setting and manner;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(3): those needs may include teachers trained in special teaching methods, small class sizes, and special materials, equipment, and classroom environments;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(4): parents are best equipped to make decisions for their children, including the educational setting that will best serve the interests and educational needs of their children;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(5): the establishment of this scholarship program is justified on the basis of funding the special needs of students with disabilities as with other programs similarly funded by the state for people with disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(6): children, parents, and families are the primary beneficiaries of the scholarship program authorized in this part and any benefit to private schools, sectarian or otherwise, is purely incidental;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(7): the scholarship program authorized in this part is:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(7)(a): enacted for the valid secular purpose of tailoring a student's education to that student's specific needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(7)(b): neutral with respect to religion;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(7)(c): provides limited assistance to citizens who are then able to direct their resources to religious and secular schools solely as a result of their genuine and independent private choices; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(7)(d): in accordance with the best interests of the taxpayers and citizens of the state to encourage educational opportunities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-301.5(8): nothing in this part shall be construed as a basis for granting vouchers or tuition tax credits for any other students, with or without disabilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302 Scholarship program created -- Qualifications.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
"I acknowledge that:Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(1): The Carson Smith Scholarship Program is created to award scholarships to students with disabilities to attend a private school.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(2): (2)(c); (3) To qualify for a scholarship:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(2)(a): the student's custodial parent shall reside within Utah;

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(2)(b)(vii): autism;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(2)(b)(viii): traumatic brain injury;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(2)(b)(ix): other health impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(2)(b)(x): specific learning disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-302(2)(b)(xi): deafblindness; or

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303 Eligible private schools.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1): (1)(f)(i); 53F-4-302(6); (1)(g); 53G-11-402; Title 53E, Chapter 6, Education Professional Licensure To be eligible to enroll a scholarship student, a private school shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(a): have a physical location in Utah where the scholarship students attend classes and have direct contact with the school's teachers;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(b)(i): contract with an independent licensed certified public accountant to conduct an Agreed Upon Procedures engagement, as adopted by the state board, or obtain an audit and report from a licensed independent certified public accountant that conforms with the following requirements:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(b)(i)(A): the audit shall be performed in accordance with generally accepted auditing standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(b)(i)(B): the financial statements shall be presented in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(b)(i)(C): the audited financial statements shall be as of a period within the last 12 months; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(b)(ii): submit the audit report or report of the agreed upon procedure to the state board when the private school applies to accept scholarship students;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(c): comply with the antidiscrimination provisions of 42 U.S.C. Sec. 2000d;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(d): meet state and local health and safety laws and codes;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(e): provide a written disclosure to the parent of each prospective student, before the student is enrolled of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(e)(i): the special education services that will be provided to the student, including the cost of those services;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(e)(ii): tuition costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(e)(iii): additional fees a parent will be required to pay during the school year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(e)(iv): the skill or grade level of the curriculum that the student will be participating in;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(f): (1)(f)(i); 53F-4-302(6)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(f)(i): administer an annual assessment of each scholarship student's academic progress;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(f)(ii): (1)(f)(i) report the results of the assessment described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(f)(iii): 53F-4-302(6) make the results available to the assessment team evaluating the student pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(g): employ or contract with teachers who:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(g)(i): hold baccalaureate or higher degrees;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(g)(ii): have at least three years of teaching experience in public or private schools; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(g)(iii): have the necessary special skills, knowledge, or expertise that qualifies them to provide instruction:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(g)(iii)(A): in the subjects taught; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(g)(iii)(B): to the special needs students taught;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(h): (1)(g) maintain documentation demonstrating that teachers at the private school meet the qualifications described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(i): 53G-11-402; Title 53E, Chapter 6, Education Professional Licensure require the following individuals to submit to a nationwide, fingerprint-based  criminal background check and ongoing monitoring, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(i)(i): Title 53E, Chapter 6, Education Professional Licensure an employee who does not hold a current Utah educator license issued by the state board under
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(i)(ii): a contract employee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(i)(iii): a volunteer who is given significant unsupervised access to a student in connection with the volunteer's assignment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(1)(j): provide to the parent of the scholarship student the relevant credentials of the teachers who will be teaching the scholarship student.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(2): (1)(b); (1)(b); (1)(b) A private school is not eligible to enroll scholarship students if:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-303(2)(a): the private school requires a student to sign a contract waiving the student's rights to transfer to another eligible private school during the school year;

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304 Scholarship payments.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1): (1)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(a): The state board shall award scholarships subject to the availability of money appropriated by the Legislature for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(b): The Legislature shall annually appropriate money to the state board from the General Fund to make scholarship payments.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(c): (1)(b) The Legislature shall annually increase the amount of money appropriated under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(c)(i): the average scholarship amount awarded as of December 1 in the previous year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(c)(ii): the product of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(c)(ii)(A): the number of students in preschool through grade 12 in public schools statewide who have an IEP on December 1 of the previous year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(c)(ii)(B): 0.0007.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(d): If the number of scholarship students as of December 1 in any school year equals or exceeds 7% of the number of students in preschool through grade 12 in public schools statewide who have an IEP as of December 1 in the same school year, the Public Education Appropriations Subcommittee shall study the requirement to increase appropriations for scholarship payments as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(e)(i): If money is not available to pay for all scholarships requested, the state board shall allocate scholarships on a random basis except that the state board shall give preference to students who received scholarships in the previous school year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(1)(e)(ii): If money is insufficient in a school year to pay for all the continuing scholarships, the state board may not award new scholarships during that school year and the state board shall prorate money available for scholarships among the eligible students who received scholarships in the previous year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(2): (4) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(2)(a): for a student who received an average of 180 minutes per day or more of special education services in a public school before transferring to a private school, an amount not to exceed the lesser of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(2)(a)(i): the value of the weighted pupil unit multiplied by 2.5; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(2)(a)(ii): the private school tuition and fees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(2)(b): for a student who received an average of less than 180 minutes per day of special education services in a public school before transferring to a private school, an amount not to exceed the lesser of:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(2)(b)(i): the value of the weighted pupil unit multiplied by 1.5; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(2)(b)(ii): the private school tuition and fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(3): (2)(a); (b) The scholarship amount for a student enrolled in a half-day kindergarten or part-day preschool program shall be the amount specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act If a student leaves a private school before the end of a fiscal quarter:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(4)(a): the private school is only entitled to the amount of scholarship equivalent to the number of days that the student attended the private school; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(4)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act the private school shall remit a prorated amount of the scholarship to the state board in accordance with the procedures described in rules adopted by the state board in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(5): (4)(b) For the amount of funds remitted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(5)(a): make the amount available to the student to enroll immediately in another qualifying private school; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-304(5)(b): refund the amount back to the Carson Smith Scholarship Program account to be available to support the costs of another scholarship.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306 Enforcement and penalties.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(1)(a): The state board shall require a private school to submit a signed affidavit assuring the private school will comply with the requirements of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(1)(b): If a school fails to submit a signed affidavit within 30 days of receiving notification that the school is an approved private school to receive the Carson Smith Scholarship, the state board may:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(1)(b)(i): deny the private school permission to enroll scholarship students; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(1)(b)(ii): interrupt disbursement of or withhold scholarship payments.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(2): The state board may investigate complaints and convene administrative hearings for an alleged violation of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(3): Upon a finding that this part was violated, the state board may:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(3)(a): deny a private school permission to enroll scholarship students;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(3)(b): interrupt disbursement of or withhold scholarship payments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-306(3)(c): issue an order for repayment of scholarship payments fraudulently obtained.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-307 Limitation on regulation of private schools.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this part grants additional authority to any state agency or LEA to regulate private schools except as expressly set forth in this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(1): 53F-4-504(1) "Authorized online course provider" means the entities listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(2): 53F-4-504(1)(a); (c)
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(2)(a): "Certified online course provider" means a provider that the state board approves to offer courses through the Statewide Online Education Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(2)(b): 53F-4-504(1)(a); (c) "Certified online course provider" does not include an entity described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(3): "Credit" means credit for a high school course, or the equivalent for a middle school course, as determined by the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(4): "Eligible student" means a student:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(4)(a): who intends to take a course for middle school or high school credit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(4)(b)(i): who is enrolled in an LEA in Utah; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(4)(b)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(4)(b)(ii)(A): who attends a private school or home school; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(4)(b)(ii)(B): whose custodial parent is a resident of Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(5): "High school" means grade 9, 10, 11, or 12.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(6): "Middle school" means, only for purposes of student eligibility to participate in the Statewide Online Education Program, grade 6, 7, or 8.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(7): "Online course" means a course of instruction offered by the Statewide Online Education Program through the use of digital technology, regardless of whether the student participates in the course at home, at school, at another location, or any combination of these.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(8): 53E-2-304 "Plan for college and career readiness" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(9): "Primary LEA of enrollment" means the LEA in which an eligible student is enrolled for courses other than online courses offered through the Statewide Online Education Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-501(10): "Released-time" means a period of time during the regular school day a student is excused from school at the request of the student's parent pursuant to rules of the state board.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502 Statewide Online Education Program created -- Designated as program of the public education system -- Purposes.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(1): The Statewide Online Education Program is created to enable an eligible student to, through the completion of publicly funded online courses:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(1)(a): earn high school graduation credit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(1)(b): earn middle school credit.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(2): Pursuant to
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3): The purposes of the Statewide Online Education Program are to:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(a): provide a student with access to online learning options regardless of where the student attends school, whether a public, private, or home school;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(b): provide digital learning options for a student regardless of language, residence, family income, or special needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(c): provide online learning options to allow a student to acquire the knowledge and technology skills necessary in a digital world;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(d): utilize the power and scalability of technology to customize education so that a student may learn in the student's own style preference and at the student's own pace;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(e): utilize technology to remove the constraints of traditional classroom learning, allowing a student to access learning virtually at any time and in any place and giving the student the flexibility to take advantage of the student's peak learning time;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(f): provide personalized learning, where a student can spend as little or as much time as the student needs to master the material;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(g): provide greater access to self-paced programs enabling a high achieving student to accelerate academically, while a struggling student may have additional time and help to gain competency;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(h): allow a student to customize the student's schedule to better meet the student's academic goals;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(i): provide quality learning options to better prepare a student for post-secondary education and vocational or career opportunities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(3)(j): allow a student to have an individualized educational experience.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-502(4): The program name, "Statewide Online Education Program," shall be used in the dissemination of information on the program.


Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-503 Option to enroll in online courses offered through the Statewide Online Education Program.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-503(1): (2); (8) Subject to Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-503(7)(b)(i)(A): instructional materials or software necessary to take an online course; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-503(7)(b)(i)(B): access to a computer or digital learning device for the purpose of taking an online course.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508 Course credit acknowledgment.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(1): A student's primary LEA of enrollment and the student's online course provider shall enter into a course credit acknowledgment in which the primary LEA of enrollment and the online course provider acknowledge that the online course provider is responsible for the instruction of the student in a specified online course.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(2): 53F-4-505; Chapter 2, State Funding -- Minimum School Program; 53F-4-505(4) The terms of the course credit acknowledgment shall provide that:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(2)(a): 53F-4-505 the online course provider shall receive a payment in the amount provided under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3): 53F-4-503; (3)(b); 53F-4-506; (3)(b); 53F-4-506
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(a): A course credit acknowledgment may originate with either an online course provider or primary LEA of enrollment.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(b): The originating entity shall submit the course credit acknowledgment to the state board who shall forward it to the primary LEA of enrollment for course selection verification or the online course provider for acceptance.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(c): 53F-4-503
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(c)(i): 53F-4-503 A primary LEA of enrollment may only reject a course credit acknowledgment if:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(c)(i)(A): the online course is not aligned with the student's plan for college and career readiness;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(c)(i)(B): the online course is not consistent with the student's IEP, if the student has an IEP;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(c)(i)(C): the online course is not consistent with the student's international baccalaureate program, if the student participates in an international baccalaureate program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(c)(i)(D): 53F-4-503 the number of online course credits exceeds the maximum allowed for the year as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(c)(ii): Verification of alignment of an online course with a student's plan for college and career readiness does not require a meeting with the student.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(d): An online course provider may only reject a course credit acknowledgment if:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(d)(i): the student does not meet course prerequisites; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(d)(ii): the course is not open for enrollment.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(e): (3)(b) A primary LEA of enrollment or online course provider shall submit an acceptance or rejection of a course credit acknowledgment to the state board within 72 business hours of the receipt of a course credit acknowledgment from the state board pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(f): 53F-4-506 If an online course provider accepts a course credit acknowledgment, the online course provider shall forward to the primary LEA of enrollment the online course start date as established under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(g): If an online course provider rejects a course credit acknowledgment, the online course provider shall include an explanation which the state board shall forward to the primary LEA of enrollment for the purpose of assisting a student with future online course selection.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(h): (3)(b) If a primary LEA of enrollment does not submit an acceptance or rejection of a course credit acknowledgment to the state board within 72 business hours of the receipt of a course credit acknowledgment from the state board pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(i): 53F-4-506
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(i)(i): 53F-4-506 Upon acceptance of a course credit acknowledgment, the primary LEA of enrollment shall notify the student of the acceptance and the start date for the online course as established under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(i)(ii): Upon rejection of a course credit acknowledgment, the primary LEA of enrollment shall notify the student of the rejection and provide an explanation of the rejection.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-4-508(3)(j): If the online course student has an individual education plan (IEP) or 504 accommodations, the primary LEA of enrollment shall forward the IEP or description of 504 accommodations to the online course provider within 72 business hours after the primary LEA of enrollment receives notice that the online course provider accepted the course credit acknowledgment.

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201 Grants for online delivery of statewide assessments.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1): 53E-4-202; 53E-4-301 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(a): "Adaptive tests" means tests administered during the school year using an online adaptive test system.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(b): 53E-4-202 "Core standards for Utah public schools" means the standards established by the state board as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(c): 53E-4-301 "Statewide assessment" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(d): "Summative tests" means tests administered near the end of a course to assess overall achievement of course goals.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(e): "Uniform online summative test system" means a single system for the online delivery of summative tests required as statewide assessments that:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(e)(i): is coordinated by the state board;
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(e)(ii): ensures the reliability and security of statewide assessments; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(1)(e)(iii): is selected through collaboration between the state board and school district representatives with expertise in technology, assessment, and administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(2): The state board may award grants to school districts and charter schools to implement:
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(2)(a): a uniform online summative test system to enable school staff and parents of students to review statewide assessment scores by the end of the school year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(2)(b): an online adaptive test system to enable parents of students and school staff to measure and monitor a student's academic progress during a school year.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(3): (3)(a)

Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(3)(a)(vi): personnel to provide technical support or coordination and management; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(3)(a)(vii): teacher professional development.
Utah Code Annotated § 53F-5-201(3)(b): (3)(a) Equipment purchased in compliance with Subsection
